#### # Instructions  
####   
#### A circular buffer, cyclic buffer or ring buffer is a data structure that uses a single, fixed-size buffer as if it were connected end-to-end.  
####   
#### A circular buffer first starts empty and of some predefined length.  
#### For example, this is a 7-element buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Assume that a 1 is written into the middle of the buffer (exact starting location does not matter in a circular buffer):  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Then assume that two more elements are added — 2 & 3 — which get appended after the 1:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][2][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If two elements are then removed from the buffer, the oldest values inside the buffer are removed.  
#### The two elements removed, in this case, are 1 & 2, leaving the buffer with just a 3:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If the buffer has 7 elements then it is completely full:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][3][4]  
#### ```  
####   
#### When the buffer is full an error will be raised, alerting the client that further writes are blocked until a slot becomes free.  
####   
#### When the buffer is full, the client can opt to overwrite the oldest data with a forced write.  
#### In this case, two more elements — A & B — are added and they overwrite the 3 & 4:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### 3 & 4 have been replaced by A & B making 5 now the oldest data in the buffer.  
#### Finally, if two elements are removed then what would be returned is 5 & 6 yielding the buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Because there is space available, if the client again uses overwrite to store C & D then the space where 5 & 6 were stored previously will be used not the location of 7 & 8.  
#### 7 is still the oldest element and the buffer is once again full.  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [C][D][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: circular_buffer.cpp circular_buffer.h  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  
####   
#### In newly generated code obey the following MISRA C++ rules:  
####   
#### <rules>  
#### The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used  
#### - Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long  
#### - Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types: std::int8_t / std::uint8_t, std::int16_t / std::uint16_t, std::int32_t / std::uint32_t, std::int64_t / std::uint64_t  
#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
####   
####   
#### The statement forming the body of an 'if' or 'else' statement should be a compound statement  
#### - Always enclose the body of every `if` and every `else` in a compound statement:    
####   `if (cond) { … }`, `else { … }`  
#### - The sole exception: `else if (cond)` is allowed without braces; all other `else` bodies need `{}`.  
#### - Do not place any statements (even one) outside braces following `if`/`else`; indentation is irrelevant.  
#### - Never add a stray semicolon after the `if (cond)` or `else` keyword; the next `{}` must start the body.  
#### - Example: instead of    
####   `if (x) doSomething();`    
####   write    
####   `if (x) { doSomething(); }`  
####   
#### The numerical value of a character shall not be used  
#### - Do not convert between character-category types (`char`, `signed/unsigned char`, `wchar_t`, `char16_t`, `char32_t`) and any non-character type (int, bool, float, enum, pointer); avoid both implicit and explicit casts.    
#### - Initialise or assign character objects only with matching character literals (e.g. `char c = '\n';`, `wchar_t w = L'x';`).    
#### - Use integer objects for numeric codes (e.g. `int code = 97;`) instead of storing them in a character object.    
#### - Never use characters in arithmetic, relational (`<`, `>`, `<=`, `>=`), logical, or boolean-context expressions; employ library helpers such as `std::char_traits<>::to_int_type()` / `to_char_type()` when numeric value access is unavoidable.    
#### - Equality comparisons `==` / `!=` between operands of the same character type are permitted; all other operations on character operands are disallowed.    
#### - Cast a character result to `void` only when discarding the return value of a function call; any other cast involving a character type violates the rule.    
#### - Using characters in unevaluated operands (`sizeof`, `decltype`, `noexcept`, `alignof`) is allowed.  
#### </rules>  
####

```cpp
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::size_t capacity);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    std::size_t head;
    std::size_t tail;
    std::size_t count;
    std::size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::size_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity_(capacity) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity_;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity_;
    count++;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity_;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity_;
        // count remains the same
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

// Explicit instantiations for common types
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<char>;
template class circular_buffer<double>;
// Add more as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, there are a few things to note:
1. The implementation uses std::size_t which is not a fixed-width type, but it's used for sizes which is appropriate
2. We need to ensure all operations follow the rules provided
3. The implementation needs to be efficient

This implementation should work according to the instructions:
- When the buffer is full, write() throws an error
- overwrite() always succeeds, replacing the oldest element when full
- read() removes and returns the oldest element, throwing if empty
- clear() resets the buffer to empty state

However, the implementation of overwrite() needs to be correct:
When the buffer is full, overwrite() should replace the oldest element (at head) and adjust head and tail
Since it's a circular buffer, both head and tail move forward when overwriting while full

This matches the example:
When the buffer is full, adding A & B overwrites 3 & 4, making 5 the oldest
So head moves to where 5 is, which is correct

Wait, in the implementation, when overwriting while full:
1. Replace the element at head with new data
2. Move head forward (oldest element is now the next one)
3. Move tail forward (since we're overwriting, the buffer stays full)
This seems correct

This implementation should work. Let's proceed.

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::size_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity_(capacity) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity_;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity_;
    count++;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1) % capacity_;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity_;
        // count remains the same
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
}

// Explicit instantiations for common types
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<char>;
template class circular_buffer<double>;
// Add more as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity_(capacity) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    count++;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

// Explicit instantiations for common types
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<char>;
template class circular_buffer<double>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity_(capacity) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    count++;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

// Explicit instantiations for common types
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<char>;
template class circular_buffer<double>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity_(capacity) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
    count--;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    count++;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = (head + 1U) % capacity_;
        tail = (tail + 1U) % capacity_;
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
```

I understand. The implementation needs to follow the MISRA C++ rules strictly. Let's fix any potential issues:

1. The implementation uses `int` which is a standard signed integer type, which violates the rules
2. We need to use fixed-width types
3. All operations need to be properly parenthesized
4. Braces need to be used for all control structures

Here are the necessary fixes:


Key changes made:
1. Replaced `int` with `std::int32_t` to use fixed-width types
2. Added extra parentheses around expressions to ensure proper precedence
3. All operations now use fixed-width integer types
4. The implementation still maintains the same functionality

This implementation should now comply with the MISRA C++ rules:
- Uses fixed-width integer types instead of standard signed integer types
- Proper parenthesization of expressions
- Braces are used for all control structures
- No mixing of integral types in assignments

Note: The implementation assumes that the data to be stored in the buffer can be represented by `std::int32_t`, which should be sufficient for the examples given (numbers and characters). If characters need to be stored, they can be cast to `std::int32_t` when writing and cast back when reading, but this should be handled by the client code.

I understand. The tests expect a template implementation, and they're trying to use different types (like `int` and `std::string`). Let's fix the implementation to be a template and handle these types correctly.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity);
    std::int32_t read();
    void write(std::int32_t data);
    void overwrite(std::int32_t data);
    void clear();
    
private:
    std::vector<std::int32_t> buffer;
    std::uint32_t head;
    std::uint32_t tail;
    std::uint32_t count;
    std::uint32_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    std::uint32_t head;
    std::uint32_t tail;
    std::uint32_t count;
    std::uint32_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity_(capacity) {
}

std::int32_t circular_buffer::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    std::int32_t value = buffer[head];
    head = ((head + 1U) % capacity_);
    count--;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(std::int32_t data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = ((tail + 1U) % capacity_);
    count++;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(std::int32_t data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = ((head + 1U) % capacity_);
        tail = ((tail + 1U) % capacity_);
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), head(0U), tail(0U), count(0U), capacity_(capacity) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (count == 0U) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = ((head + 1U) % capacity_);
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (count == capacity_) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = ((tail + 1U) % capacity_);
    count++;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (count < capacity_) {
        write(data);
    } else {
        buffer[head] = data;
        head = ((head + 1U) % capacity_);
        tail = ((tail + 1U) % capacity_);
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0U;
    tail = 0U;
    count = 0U;
}

// Explicit instantiations
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<std::string>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Key changes made:
1. Made the implementation a template to support different types
2. Added `const T&` parameters to write and overwrite to handle various types efficiently
3. Added explicit instantiations for `int` and `std::string` to satisfy the tests
4. Kept the core functionality the same

This should now work with the tests that are trying to use both integers and strings. The implementation follows the same logic as before, just generalized to work with any type.

```cpp
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <cstdint>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <vector>
#include <string>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(std::uint32_t capacity);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    std::uint32_t head;
    std::uint32_t tail;
    std::uint32_t count;
    std::uint32_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This change adds the `<string>` header which is needed for the explicit instantiation of `circular_buffer<std::string>` in the implementation file. The rest of the implementation remains the same and should now compile correctly.
